# Executive framing
## Assumptions
- Audience: early to growth-stage mobile game founders and studio leaders building investor-grade decks for Seed, Series A, and diligence processes.
- Scope: mobile F2P as baseline with room for hybrid monetisation. Guidance adapts to Telegram Mini Apps, iOS, Android, Poki web, and Steam via a platform annex.
- Benchmarks: use industry reports for 2025 where public data exists; treat ranges as directional and calibrate by genre and geo. citeturn0search3turn5search1

## Brief plan
1. Set quality bar and visual standards.  
2. Provide slide count and pacing guidance.  
3. Teach Seed, Series A, and Due Diligence decks slide by slide: what to show, why it matters, how to build it.  
4. Add tutorials for narrative, KPIs, and measurement changes in 2025.  
5. Add platform annex with experiment gates.  
6. Close with checklists, scoring rubrics, and acronym glossary.

## Deliverable
A single, teach-through guide you can hand to a first-time founder and expect a competent, investor-ready deck at each stage.

## Self-audit
- Freshness: 2024–2025 sources for investor behaviour, platform policies, and measurement changes are cited inline.  
- Readability: concise bullets, British English, no dividers, no icons, no em dashes.  
- Actionability: every slide includes content checklist, narrative intent, and pitfalls.

---

# Quality bar and visual fidelity

## The reality of investor attention
- Investors typically skim a deck in under 3 minutes on first read, so slides must be legible and scannable with a strong narrative. Multiple studies of deck telemetry show average time on deck between about 2:20 and 3:00 and falling year over year. Design clarity improves outcomes. citeturn0search22turn0search10turn0search2

## Visual standards
- Type: one display face for headings, one highly legible text face for body. Minimum 24 pt body, 36–48 pt headings.  
- Colour: 1 primary, 1 accent, 1 neutral. Maintain contrast ratios suitable for accessibility.  
- Layout: one message per slide. Headline that reads as a sentence. Evidence in one chart or two concise bullets.  
- Imagery: only in-engine captures or relevant UI. No clip art.  
- Charts: avoid pies. Prefer bars, line charts with labelled points, and small-multiples for cohorts.  
- Motion: keep to simple fades. Do not rely on animations to convey meaning.  
- Craft: align elements to a grid, maintain equal spacing, set consistent margins, and lock a baseline grid.  
- File hygiene: export a PDF under 15 MB for email and a PowerPoint or Keynote for live.

---

# Slide count and pacing
- Target 10 to 15 slides for Seed and Series A. This range is consistently recommended by leading accelerators and investors and reflects how quickly decks are skimmed. citeturn0search0turn0search4  
- Due Diligence materials are not a deck alone. Expect a 15 to 25 slide diligence overview plus linked appendices and a data room index.

---

# Seed deck: slide-by-slide tutorial

> Goal: make it obvious there is a real problem, a differentiated solution, a credible audience, an initial traction signal or prototype, and a team who can get to product-market fit.

1) Title and promise  
- What: company name, one-line purpose, platform targets.  
- Why: investors decide relevance in seconds. Use a declarative purpose line. citeturn0search13  
- Build: logo, purpose, short descriptor, funding ask and use of funds in one line.

2) Problem or need  
- What: the pain for the player or the buyer.  
- Why: anchors value and market pull.  
- Build: two bullets with evidence or a single insight chart.

3) Solution and product  
- What: your core loop and differentiators.  
- Why: connects directly to the problem.  
- Build: a single annotated screenshot or short loop diagram with one sentence on why it is hard to copy.

4) Why now  
- What: timing drivers such as distribution shifts, ad-privacy changes, or platform terms that unlock your approach.  
- Why: investors back timing as much as teams. citeturn0search13  
- Build: three drivers with a short benefit line for each.

5) Market  
- What: bottom-up reachable audience and spend, not just top-down TAM.  
- Why: shows commercial headroom.  
- Build: simple pyramid TAM to SAM to SOM with your near-term wedge. If platform-specific, point to annex.

6) Traction or proof  
- What: prototypes, early tests, playtests, waitlist, or channel experiments.  
- Why: reduces risk.  
- Build: one metric panel with definitions. Use reputable benchmarks for context. GameAnalytics publish retention bands by genre each year; frame your D1, D7, and D28 against those bands. citeturn0search3

7) Business model  
- What: your revenue mix and payer journey.  
- Why: links game design to income.  
- Build: IAP ladder concept, price points, soft vs hard currency, starter bundle, and expected payer share. If ad-supported, show ad surfaces.

8) Go-to-market  
- What: first channels and learning plan as experiments with gates.  
- Why: avoids big-bet distribution.  
- Build: list 2 to 3 tests you will run next with success thresholds. Use the platform annex for gates.

9) Competition  
- What: the player’s choice set and your asymmetric edge.  
- Why: shows you understand the field.  
- Build: do not use a vendor quadrant unless genuinely data-backed. A comparison table of features and moat is clearer.

10) Team  
- What: why you are the right team to win.  
- Why: capability and speed are central at Seed.  
- Build: 3 to 5 bios with shipped titles, measurable outcomes, or relevant network effects.

11) Plan and use of funds  
- What: milestones for the next 18 months.  
- Why: maps money to risk retirement.  
- Build: a quarter-by-quarter lane view with two or three crisp milestones per lane.

12) The ask  
- What: amount, instrument, and room left.  
- Why: set expectations and timeline.  
- Build: one line on how this round gets you to a de-risked Series A story.

Common Seed pitfalls  
- Overloaded slides, jargon, or unclear loop.  
- Market size hand-waving.  
- Distribution treated as a foregone conclusion instead of testable channel experiments.

---

# Series A deck: slide-by-slide tutorial

> Goal: demonstrate repeatable traction, unit economics trending toward profitability, a credible growth engine, and readiness to scale.

1) Title and state of the business  
- Include installs, MAU, revenue run rate, and latest growth rate in one band.

2) Narrative of progress  
- A single timeline from prototype to the present. Include weekly or monthly improvements tied to experiments.

3) Product and economy deep dive  
- Show live-ops cadence, economy sinks and sources, early payer arcs, and stability of ARPPU.

4) Traction metrics  
- Present D1, D7, D30, 30-day ARPDAU, pay conversion, and refund rate. Use current market benchmarks to contextualise the numbers. citeturn0search3

5) Unit economics and path to scale  
- LTV by cohort, CAC by channel, payback, and sensitivity. Keep SKAdNetwork and Android Privacy Sandbox constraints in mind for attribution windows and reporting. citeturn1search1turn1search2

6) Go-to-market engine  
- Channel mix and creative system. Note platform policy realities in 2025: iOS attribution via SKAdNetwork and AdAttributionKit, and EU alternative terms with Core Technology Fee for those who opt in. citeturn1search1turn1search0turn1search4

7) Team and hiring plan  
- Where seniority is added to de-risk scale.

8) Financial model  
- Traction-anchored forecast with drivers, not static numbers. Align scenarios with platform fees and attribution changes. citeturn1search2

9) Risks and mitigations  
- Product, platform, and capital risks with specific next actions.

10) The ask and use of proceeds  
- Scale plan to profitability or to the next clear financing milestone.

Common Series A pitfalls  
- Over-indexing on vanity metrics.  
- Ignoring 2025 attribution realities or EU fee structures that change net revenue on iOS. citeturn1search0

---

# Due Diligence deck: structure and contents

> Goal: provide a clean map of the business with links into the data room.

1) Company overview  
- Legal entities, cap table summary, IP ownership status.

2) Product and tech  
- Architecture, data model, SDKs, privacy and compliance posture. In the UK, you must consider the Online Safety Act if your service has user interaction or UGC features. Provide your compliance plan and risk register. citeturn1search3turn1search15

3) Market and competition  
- Evidence sources, share of voice, and moat.

4) Go-to-market  
- Paid, organic, community, and partnerships.

5) Data and analytics  
- Event taxonomy, cohorting, SKAN schema mapping and Android Privacy Sandbox reporting. citeturn1search1turn1search2

6) Financials  
- Historical P&L, cash runway, accrual policies, revenue recognition, and scenario drivers.

7) Operational readiness  
- Hiring plan, vendors, security practices, and incident processes.

8) Governance and risk  
- Open risks, mitigations, and decision log.

9) Appendices index  
- A linked table of contents into the data room.

---

# Tutorials

## Writing the narrative
- Slide headlines should tell the story on their own. Investors recommend story headlines over bland labels. citeturn0search5  
- Each slide answers one question in the mind of the reader. Read your deck by headlines only to check flow.

## Selecting KPIs and benchmarks
- Use retention and monetisation bands from current industry benchmarks to judge fitness. GameAnalytics publish annual retention distributions by genre. Keep in mind that medians sit below top quartile numbers. citeturn0search3turn0search19

## Attribution and measurement in 2025
- iOS: design for SKAdNetwork and AdAttributionKit. Plan coarse and fine conversion values and multiple postbacks in SKAN 4+. citeturn1search1turn1search5  
- Android: plan for the Privacy Sandbox Attribution Reporting APIs and reporting lags. citeturn1search2turn1search6

## Market context snapshots you can cite
- Mobile gaming returned to growth into 2025, with reported IAP revenue and engagement up in aggregate year over year. Use this as context, not as a promise for any one title. citeturn5search1turn5search5

# Platform annex: channel-specific guidance and KPI gates

> Use distribution surfaces as experiments, not assumptions. Copy the template, run a 2 to 4 week test, then scale or stop.

## Experiment design template
- Objective, audience and geo, entry points, tracking plan, creative set, budget caps, success gates, next action.

## Telegram Mini Apps
- What matters: distribution comes through channels, groups, deep links, and Telegram Ads. Mini Apps are JS web apps that can run fullscreen, with integrated payments via Stars for digital goods. citeturn2search2turn2news28turn2search0  
- Payments: Stars for digital goods and subs; see Bot Payments and Stars docs. Third-party options vary by goods type. citeturn2search3  
- KPI gates, 2-week alpha: start rate from land ≥ 60 percent, FTUE ≥ 70 percent, D1 ≥ 30 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.0 percent or sub attach ≥ 0.5 percent, viral K ≥ 0.15, Stars refunds < 2 percent.  
- Notes: treat as web analytics with UTM deep links and server events. Ads run in broadcast channels 1,000+ subs. citeturn2search1

## Poki web
- What matters: staged Player Fit Test (~500 players) then Web Fit Test with Poki traffic before monetisation SDK use. Rewarded and commercial breaks are integrated after testing phases. citeturn3search3turn3search0  
- KPI gates: category CTR top quartile, conversion to first gameplay high, median first session 6 to 10 minutes depending on genre, time-to-first-interaction target under a few seconds; then ad break acceptance once SDK is live. citeturn3search1turn3search12

## iOS App Store
- What matters: attribution via SKAdNetwork and AdAttributionKit. In the EU, alternative terms introduce the Core Technology Fee for developers who opt in under DMA. Factor fee modelling into net revenue. citeturn1search1turn1search4turn1search0  
- KPI gates, soft launch: D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent mid-core reference, tutorial completion ≥ 80 percent, pay conversion ≥ 1.5 percent or sub trial ≥ 2.5 percent. Benchmarks are directional and must be calibrated by genre. citeturn0search3

## Android
- What matters: Privacy Sandbox replaces cross-party IDs with on-device APIs, changing attribution and reporting cadence. citeturn1search2  
- KPI gates, soft launch: use same retention targets as iOS for mid-core, track Sandbox windows, and use proxy ROAS measures with confidence bands until revenue settles.

## Steam
- What matters: wishlists, demo performance, and Next Fest momentum. Steam’s revenue share drops at 10 million and 50 million lifetime gross. citeturn4search1turn4search3  
- KPI gates: pre-launch wishlists in the tens of thousands for meaningful premium launches, Next Fest demo-to-wishlist conversion as a key signal, and review score targets post-launch. Use Valve’s official Next Fest documentation to plan timing. citeturn4search1

# Build-this-slide recipes

For each slide below, apply: headline that reads as a sentence, one chart or image, two bullets of proof.

## Seed: traction slide recipe
- Chart: weekly D1 and D7 lines with annotations for each experiment.  
- Bullets: one plain-English learning and one next action.  
- Footer: cohort sizes and definitions. Compare to current genre benchmarks. citeturn0search3

## Series A: unit economics slide recipe
- Chart: cohort LTV vs CAC by channel with payback bands.  
- Bullets: what moved LTV and what moved CAC.  
- Footer: attribution method by platform and any limits due to SKAN or Sandbox windows. citeturn1search1turn1search2

## Due Diligence: compliance slide recipe
- Table: platform, policy area, status.  
- Bullets: evidence links to policies and your controls. Include Online Safety Act if you have UGC or interaction. citeturn1search3

# Quality checklists and rubrics

## One-minute skim test
- Read only slide headlines in order. If the story lands cleanly, pass. If not, rewrite headlines.

## Readability checklist
- 1 idea per slide  
- Minimum 24 pt body  
- Max 2 evidence bullets  
- Charts labelled; axes units clear  
- File size < 15 MB PDF export

## Visual polish checklist
- Grid alignment consistent  
- Equal spacing and margins  
- Alt text set for images in the source file  
- Colour contrast meets accessibility guidance

## Content completeness gates
- Seed: problem, solution, market, early proof, GTM tests, team, ask.  
- Series A: product stability, growth engine, unit economics, scale plan, hiring, risks.  
- Diligence: full data room index with links.

## Scoring rubric, 1 to 10
- Quality of narrative  
- Accuracy of claims and sources  
- Detail level versus stage  
- Readability and visual polish  
- Likely retention and recall

---

# Acronyms and definitions

- ARPPU: Average Revenue Per Paying User.  
- ARPDAU: Average Revenue Per Daily Active User.  
- ATT: AppTrackingTransparency, iOS permission framework.  
- CAC: Customer Acquisition Cost.  
- CTF: Core Technology Fee under Apple EU alternative terms for those who opt in. citeturn1search0  
- D1, D7, D28, D30: Day-based retention checkpoints. Benchmarks vary by genre and platform. citeturn0search3  
- DMA: EU Digital Markets Act, driving Apple’s EU alternative terms. citeturn1search12  
- FTUE: First Time User Experience.  
- KPI: Key Performance Indicator.  
- LTV: Lifetime Value per user or per install, cohort-based.  
- ROAS: Return on Ad Spend.  
- SKAN: SKAdNetwork, iOS privacy-preserving attribution framework. citeturn1search1  
- UGC: User-generated content.  
- UTM: Urchin Tracking Module parameters for links.  
- VC: Venture Capitalist.

## B. Platform quick-reference gates
| Platform | Pass gates to continue |
|---|---|
| Telegram Mini App | Start ≥ 60 percent, FTUE ≥ 70 percent, D1 ≥ 30 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.0 percent or sub attach ≥ 0.5 percent, K ≥ 0.15, refunds < 2 percent |
| Poki | Category CTR top quartile, conversion to play high, median first session ≥ 6–10 minutes, TTFI short, then rewarded and commercial breaks acceptance after SDK |
| iOS | D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent mid-core reference, tutorial ≥ 80 percent, pay conversion ≥ 1.5 percent or sub trial ≥ 2.5 percent, compliance clean |
| Android | Same retention targets by genre, Sandbox attribution configured, Day-7 proxy ROAS credible with confidence bands |
| Steam | Meaningful wishlist base, Next Fest demo-to-wishlist conversion strong, positive review velocity, revenue share tiers understood |

# Universal narrative spine and slide count policy

## Narrative beats investors expect
- Purpose
- Why now
- Market and opportunity
- Product and core loop
- Business model and economy
- Distribution and GTM
- Competition
- Team
- Roadmap and milestones
- Financials and use of funds
- Risks and mitigations
- The Ask

## Slide count and pacing
- Live Seed or Series A: 10–15 slides for the core narrative.
- Send-ahead PDF: 12–18 slides for the core, with appendices for tables and cohorts.
- Due Diligence: a 15–25 slide overview plus a linked data room.

---

# Seed deck tutorial: full slide-by-slide build

For each slide below: Objective, What to show, Why it matters, Inputs and assets, Visual spec, Quality checks, Pitfalls.

1) Cover  
- Objective: Set promise and context in 3 seconds.  
- What to show: Studio name, one-line promise, platform focus, founders, contact. One striking in-engine image or a muted 5–10 second loop.  
- Why it matters: Frames the category and quality bar instantly.  
- Inputs and assets: Logo, key art or gameplay clip, contact line.  
- Visual spec: 16:9 at 1920×1080, safe margins 40 px; grid (12-column or simple 4-column); Title ≥ 40 pt; Headings ≥ 28 pt; Body ≥ 20 pt; Labels ≥ 16 pt.  
- Quality checks: Ultra-readable title; legal-cleared image; file sizes optimised.  
- Pitfalls: Concept art that is not representative of gameplay.

2) Why now  
- Objective: Show the timing edge.  
- What to show: Three dated timing drivers such as distribution shifts, UA landscape changes, genre fatigue, or new monetisation mechanics. One compact chart or timeline.  
- Why it matters: Investors look for market inflections, not static markets.  
- Inputs and assets: Two to three data points with dates; a one-year timeline.  
- Visual spec: One chart; one sentence per driver.  
- Quality checks: Each driver tied to a concrete outcome like lower CPI, higher watch-time, higher payer rate.  
- Pitfalls: Vague trends or stale data.

3) Opportunity  
- Objective: Quantify realistic upside.  
- What to show: TAM for mobile games, then a defendable sub-genre SAM and your initial SOM by channel and geo. One bar chart and a single sentence on reachability.  
- Why it matters: Rightsizes ambition to an executable plan.  
- Inputs and assets: Market numbers with sources and dates; peer benchmarks.  
- Visual spec: Bars with labelled units and dates; SOM derived bottom-up.  
- Quality checks: SOM is defendable, not a flat percentage of TAM.  
- Pitfalls: Stacking overlapping markets or using unlabelled geos.

4) Problem and player insight  
- Objective: Prove you understand your player.  
- What to show: Two frictions and two desires, each paired with a clip or quote. Define audience segment and play occasion.  
- Why it matters: Accurate insight predicts retention.  
- Inputs and assets: Playtest notes; community posts; short reels of reference behaviours.  
- Visual spec: Two tiles; captions ≤ 15 words; readable on laptop and boardroom screen.  
- Quality checks: Insights specific to the sub-genre; not generic fun statements.  
- Pitfalls: Personas without behavioural proof.

5) The game: 15-second hook  
- Objective: Communicate the core in one breath.  
- What to show: One-sentence pitch; 15-second continuous gameplay montage; genre; camera; primary interaction; average session length; platform.  
- Why it matters: This is where excitement starts or ends.  
- Inputs and assets: Capture from a working build; no cinematic cuts that hide inputs.  
- Visual spec: 1080p MP4; ≤ 15 MB; HUD visible if it clarifies the loop.  
- Quality checks: Clip shows actual control and feedback loop; HUD readable.  
- Pitfalls: Teaser trailers with no input feedback.

6) Core loop and systems  
- Objective: Show how fun compounds into retention and spend.  
- What to show: Loop diagram with 3–5 verbs; two deepening systems such as progression or events; one sentence on how they create mastery and economy sinks.  
- Why it matters: Loops generate the economics.  
- Inputs and assets: Loop schematic; economy sinks and sources list; sample screens.  
- Visual spec: One loop schematic; two small callouts; consistent icons and labels.  
- Quality checks: Loop fits declared session length; systems are additive, not bloating.  
- Pitfalls: Five or more systems before soft launch.

7) Distribution advantage  
- Objective: Prove access to players beyond spend.  
- What to show: Primary channels; creative angles; community and creator leverage; any exclusive placements. One small table: channel, cost target, expected scale.  
- Why it matters: Distribution is often the real moat.  
- Inputs and assets: Creator list; community plan; placement conversations.  
- Visual spec: Clean table ≤ 6 rows; one supporting graphic if needed.  
- Quality checks: At least one non-paid growth lever with a testable plan.  
- Pitfalls: Assuming paid UA will always be available at the modelled CPI.

8) Monetisation model  
- Objective: Show value exchange and pricing logic.  
- What to show: Primary pillars like cosmetic IAPs, gacha, BP; price bands; early shop mockups; ad strategy if used; guardrails to avoid pay-to-win.  
- Why it matters: Trust and clarity drive payer rate.  
- Inputs and assets: SKUs table; price ladders; sample bundles; UX wireframes.  
- Visual spec: One store mockup; one SKU ladder table.  
- Quality checks: First purchase path is obvious; soft-currency sinks sized to session cadence.  
- Pitfalls: Copying a top grossing store without matching cadence or audience.

9) Early metrics or model  
- Objective: Anchor on data, or show an honest model if pre-data.  
- What to show: If tested, D1, D7, D30, ARPDAU, payer rate, first purchase time, by source. If pre-live, show a transparent LTV model with benchmarks and sensitivity ranges.  
- Why it matters: Investors underwrite to curves, not adjectives.  
- Inputs and assets: Cohort tables; source tags; model sheet.  
- Visual spec: One lead chart; one small cohort table; axes labelled; units and dates visible.  
- Quality checks: Cohorts not blended; sensitivity ± 20 percent on key drivers.  
- Pitfalls: Cherry picking best cohorts only.

10) Go to market  
- Objective: Show the first 180-day learning plan.  
- What to show: Soft-launch plan with 2 test geos; creative testing framework; community beats; creator plan; referral mechanics; PR moments; measurement plan by channel.  
- Why it matters: Speed to learning reduces capital needed.  
- Inputs and assets: Calendar; creative backlog; test matrices; Discord plan; SKAN schema mapping; Android Privacy Sandbox test plan.  
- Visual spec: One timetable; one method box listing attribution per channel.  
- Quality checks: Each test has a decision rule and owner; stop rules documented.  
- Pitfalls: Long launch with no hard gates.

11) Competitive landscape  
- Objective: Position clearly against real substitutes.  
- What to show: 3–5 nearest comps; your wedge in fun, distribution, or economics. One matrix with one dimension per axis that actually varies.  
- Why it matters: Investors scan for crowdedness and differentiation.  
- Inputs and assets: Comp feature grid; revenue ranks; review snippets.  
- Visual spec: Simple 2×2 or feature table; three callouts.  
- Quality checks: Wedge is felt in the loop, not only a brand statement.  
- Pitfalls: Giant 9×9 grids with everyone in the centre.

12) Team  
- Objective: De-risk execution with relevant wins.  
- What to show: 4–6 core leaders; two lines that tie to shipped titles or scaled live ops; advisory board only if hands on.  
- Why it matters: Pre-seed and seed are team bets.  
- Inputs and assets: Bios; shipped games list; role coverage map.  
- Visual spec: Consistent headshot ratio; tiles aligned to grid.  
- Quality checks: Roles map to loop, economy, live ops, data, and UA.  
- Pitfalls: Long biographies or celebrity advisors with no time allocation.

13) Roadmap and stage-gated milestones  
- Objective: Align capital to outcomes.  
- What to show: Past proof points with dates; next four gates with exit criteria, KPIs, and test plans. Examples: First Playable, Closed Alpha, Soft-launch 1 and 2, Global Launch Candidate.  
- Why it matters: Investors commit to gates.  
- Inputs and assets: Milestone plan; KPI targets; risk owners.  
- Visual spec: Milestone timeline with KPIs beside each gate.  
- Quality checks: Each gate has a measurable KPI like D1, D7, FTUE completion, payback.  
- Pitfalls: Vague milestones like polish or improve retention.

14) Financial plan snapshot  
- Objective: Present burn and runway tied to plan.  
- What to show: 18–24 month budget by function; hiring tranches; third parties; infra; UA runway; cash burn; runway months; unit economics summary like target LTV by cohort and payback.  
- Why it matters: Validates ask size and survivability.  
- Inputs and assets: Headcount plan; vendor quotes; UA assumptions.  
- Visual spec: One line chart for burn; one small unit-economics table.  
- Quality checks: Month-by-month burn reconciles; hiring matches milestones; UA spend only when retention gates clear.  
- Pitfalls: Flat headcount lines or UA before retention gates.

15) EU distribution and fees summary  
- Objective: Reflect EU 2025 realities without bloating the core.  
- What to show: iOS EU distribution options and fee components; Android fee options where applicable. One comparison table and a short note that the full fee model lives in the appendix.  
- Why it matters: Net revenue and margin depend on fee choices.  
- Inputs and assets: EU terms references; your fee scenario worksheet.  
- Visual spec: Two columns; clear footnotes; dates on sources.  
- Quality checks: Totals reconcile to the financial model; show assumptions.  
- Pitfalls: Ignoring EU distribution choices or mixing gross and net.

16) Risks and mitigations  
- Objective: Build trust by naming the dragons.  
- What to show: Top 5 risks across product, UA, tech, compliance, team; one line mitigation and owner each.  
- Why it matters: Shows maturity and speeds diligence.  
- Inputs and assets: Risk register; owners; contingency costs.  
- Visual spec: Five rows; owner and next check column.  
- Quality checks: Risks are specific and testable.  
- Pitfalls: Generic business clichés.

17) The Ask  
- Objective: Make it easy to say yes.  
- What to show: Round size; instrument; timing; lead or committed if any; use of proceeds line; data room link; contact.  
- Why it matters: Closes the loop and sets the next step.  
- Inputs and assets: Term targets; timeline; data room.  
- Visual spec: Large, clear contact line.

---

# Series A deck tutorial: full slide-by-slide build

1) Cover  
- Objective: Consistent identity and state.  
- What to show: Studio name; one-line promise; current install base; MAU; revenue run rate.  
- Why it matters: Sets scale immediately.  
- Inputs and assets: Live KPIs and growth rate.

2) Why now update  
- Objective: Show platform and market motion since Seed.  
- What to show: Two to three shifts that affect UA, fees, geo strategy.  
- Why it matters: Revalidates timing.

3) Traction summary  
- Objective: One-page traction snapshot.  
- What to show: Installs; DAU or MAU; payers; revenue mix; top geos; lead curve for retention or payback.  
- Inputs and assets: Cohort-based metrics.

4) Product deep dive  
- Objective: What sustains D30 and beyond.  
- What to show: Systems and live-ops cadence that create durable engagement; economy sinks and sources; example content cadence.  
- Inputs and assets: Mode map; cadence calendar; economy diagram.

5) Cohorts and retention curves  
- Objective: Prove repeatability.  
- What to show: D1, D7, D28 or D30 by source and platform; curve shapes and dispersion.  
- Inputs and assets: Cohort exports; source and platform tags.  
- Visual spec: Small multiples or layered curves with clear legend.  
- Quality checks: No blended curves; units and dates labelled.

6) Monetisation deep dive  
- Objective: Show store architecture and conversion funnel.  
- What to show: SKU ladder; first-purchase path; price tests; ad stack contribution; refund rate.  
- Inputs and assets: Store mockups; funnel; A/B logs.

7) Unit economics  
- Objective: Prove scalable economics by channel.  
- What to show: LTV by cohort and channel; CAC by channel; LTV:CAC; payback windows with sensitivity.  
- Inputs and assets: Cohort revenue by channel; CAC logs; fee model assumptions.  
- Visual spec: Payback chart per channel with error bands; one mini-table.  
- Quality checks: Methods labelled per channel; not blended.

8) GTM engine  
- Objective: Show a repeatable growth machine.  
- What to show: Channel mix; creative taxonomy; volume; win-rate; refresh cadence; scale constraints; creator programmes; community operations.  
- Inputs and assets: Creative backlog; hypothesis log; channel caps.

9) Technology and operations  
- Objective: De-risk scale and uptime.  
- What to show: Build pipeline; analytics; experiment framework; live-ops tooling; compliance posture.  
- Inputs and assets: Stack diagram; ownership map; SDK list.

10) Roadmap and scale plan  
- Objective: Tie funding to scale work.  
- What to show: New markets; content cadence; feature bets; infra scale; AB testing roadmap with decision rules.  
- Inputs and assets: Timeline and KPI gates.

11) Team for scale  
- Objective: Show upgraded coverage.  
- What to show: Key hires since Seed and open roles mapped to scale risks; seniority and ownership areas.  
- Inputs and assets: Org map and role specs.

12) Financials  
- Objective: Show build, operate, grow.  
- What to show: Revenue; gross margin drivers; burn; runway; plan; scenario drivers; fee and policy impacts in EU.  
- Inputs and assets: Financial model; fee workbook; attribution limits.

13) EU distribution and fees impact  
- Objective: Reflect margin impact of 2025 fee options.  
- What to show: iOS EU options and fee components; Android terms where applicable; one margin bridge from gross to net.  
- Inputs and assets: Fee scenario worksheet.

14) Risks and mitigations  
- Objective: Name concentration, policy, content velocity, tech debt.  
- What to show: Five rows; owners; mitigations; checkpoint dates.

15) The Ask  
- Objective: Tie raise to scale plan.  
- What to show: Round size; timing; data room link; hiring tranche table reference.

---

# Due Diligence deck: structure and contents

1) Executive summary  
- Objective: Three to five bullets with links to sections.  
- Visual: One page of links.

2) Company and legal  
- Contents: Org chart; cap table; equity plans; key contracts; licences; IP assignments.  
- Visual: Tabular glossary and link list.

3) Product and roadmap  
- Contents: Design docs; live-ops calendars; feature backlogs; pipelines; release process.

4) Data and analytics  
- Contents: Event taxonomy; cohort exports by geo, source, platform, version; retention and revenue curves; attribution method noted per cut; SKAN schema; Privacy Sandbox test summaries.  
- Visual: Annotated charts with labelled units, currency, and dates.

5) Go-to-market  
- Contents: UA test logs; channel performance; creative taxonomy and results; creator programmes; community ops; store listing experiments.

6) Financials  
- Contents: Historical P&L; cash flow; forecasts; budget by function; vendor schedules; UA spend logs; margin bridges that reflect platform fees.

7) Technology  
- Contents: Architecture; SDK list; CI pipeline; security practices; compliance notes; data retention and privacy.

8) People  
- Contents: Bios; hiring plan; contractors; compensation bands; coverage gaps.

9) Risks and compliance  
- Contents: Risk register; mitigations; policy alignment; data privacy; Online Safety Act posture for UGC or chat; age-assurance plan and vendor; moderation workflows; EU DMA choices and fee tier rationale.

10) Appendices  
- Store pages; reviews; customer support tags; platform communications; legal correspondences.

---

# Visual and fidelity guide: full spec

## 1) Foundations
- Canvas: 16:9 at 1920×1080. Safe margins: 40 px all sides. Use a 12-column grid or a simple 4-column grid with 24 px gutters.  
- Palette: 1 primary, 1 secondary, 1 highlight, 2 neutrals. Limit categories in any one chart to 6. Reserve highlight for the single idea on the slide.  
- Type: one sans-serif family only. Title ≥ 40 pt, headings ≥ 28 pt, body ≥ 20 pt, labels ≥ 16 pt. Line spacing 1.15 to 1.3. Avoid all caps for paragraphs.  
- Contrast: meet WCAG AA. Aim for a contrast ratio of 4.5:1 or higher on text.  
- Density: one message per slide, 3 to 5 short lines, 1 graphic max.

## 2) Imagery and video
- Gameplay: capture from a working build. Resolution 1080p. Show input and feedback, not cinematics. Trim to 15 seconds for the hook slide and keep total video under 30 seconds across the deck.  
- Compression: H.264 MP4, under 15 MB per clip. Static images at 150–200 DPI, PNG for UI, JPEG for full-bleed backgrounds under 400 KB each.  
- Framing: include HUD when it communicates mechanics. Avoid tilt and dutch angles unless part of the game camera.

## 3) Charts and tables
- Prefer bars, lines, waterfalls, cohort curves, and funnels. Avoid pies.  
- Axes start at zero unless a clipped axis is explicitly marked. Always label units, currency, and dates.  
- Annotate insight directly on the chart in one short line. Keep gridlines faint. No 3D.  
- Tables: max 6 rows by 4 columns in the core deck. Larger tables go to the appendix.

## 4) Slide patterns by purpose
- Cover: single image or short gameplay loop. Title and one-line promise. Founder names small at bottom.  
- The game hook: 15-second clip, one-sentence pitch, 3 tags only (genre, camera, session length).  
- Core loop: simple loop diagram with 3 to 5 verbs, plus two callouts for systems that deepen mastery.  
- Market and why now: one chart each, one callout each. Do not stack more than 2 charts on a single slide.  
- Monetisation: store mockup plus a tidy SKU ladder. One callout states the first purchase path.  
- Metrics: one lead chart (D1, D7, D30 or payback) with a small table of supporting numbers.  
- Team: 4 to 6 tiles, each with a title, shipped game, and a single outcome line.  
- Risks: 5 rows only, each with an owner and mitigation.

## 5) Animation and motion
- Keep to simple appear or fade animations. Duration 200 to 300 ms. Max 2 animations per slide. No fly-ins or spins.  
- Use builds to reveal complex charts stepwise during live talks, but export the final static state to PDF.

## 6) Accessibility and readability
- Colour-only distinctions must also have labels or patterns.  
- Never put text directly over busy imagery. Use a 70 to 85 percent black or white overlay behind text when needed.  
- Provide concise alt text in speaker notes for key visuals when the PDF may be reviewed with assistive tech.

## 7) Brand and UI discipline
- Consistent placement: titles top-left; source line bottom-right; slide number bottom-centre.  
- Consistent iconography policy: avoid decorative icons. Use short labels instead.  
- Do not mix rounded and sharp UI shapes on the same slide unless it mirrors in-game UI.

## 8) File hygiene
- Master template only. Define title, content, section divider, and appendix masters before build.  
- Versioning: DeckName_vMajor.Minor_Date. Keep a change log in the appendix first page.  
- Exports: PDF ≤ 12–15 MB. Ensure embedded fonts. Provide a link to the live presentation copy for meetings.

## 9) QA checklist per slide
- Message: one clear takeaway, stated in the title.  
- Evidence: at least one dated source, metric, or real capture that supports the takeaway.  
- Readability: body text ≥ 20 pt, adequate line spacing, clean margins.  
- Visuals: no more than one primary graphic. Palette adheres to the 5-colour limit.  
- Data hygiene: units and time bases labelled, axes correct, sources included in 10 pt at bottom-right.  
- Consistency: aligns with template grid, title position, footer, and numbering.

## 10) Acceptance rubric (0 to 5)
- 5: Investor-ready. Clear message, clean visual hierarchy, accurate data, flawless spacing, strong evidence.  
- 4: Minor tweaks only. One spacing or sizing issue, or a small labelling fix.  
- 3: Needs revision. Clutter, weak contrast, or unclear message.  
- 2: Major issues. Mixed fonts, poor data labelling, busy layout, unclear evidence.  
- 1: Unusable. Violates core standards, unreadable, or misleading charting.

---

# Evidence, metrics, and references for games

Use as context in notes or appendix; do not claim medians as targets without genre and geo nuance.

- Retention context: D1, D7, D28 bands by genre and region from current industry benchmarks.  
- Monetisation patterns: ARPU differences by model and platform to inform SKU ladders and projections.  
- UA and creative trends: creative win-rate and concentration; use a creative testing system and log hypotheses.  
- Market motion: 2024 to 2025 return to growth in mobile with regional variance.

---

# Platform Annex: channel-specific guidance and KPI gates

How to use: pick a platform; copy the experiment design; run a 2–4 week test; judge with pass/fail gates; scale if you pass.

## Experiment design template
- Objective: what decision this test must unlock.  
- Audience and geo: target cohort, language, store region.  
- Entry points: where traffic starts on the platform.  
- Tracking: legal and technical measurement stack.  
- Creative set: number of variants and hooks.  
- Budget and caps: ceiling per day and per variant.  
- Success gates: thresholds listed below.  
- Next action: scale plan if gates are met.

### Telegram Mini Apps
- What matters: distribution via channels, groups, bot discovery, deep links, and Telegram Ads. Mini Apps are Web Apps that launch inside Telegram with JS APIs for auth, payments, fullscreen, theming, and device capabilities. Stars enable in-Telegram purchases for digital goods and subscriptions.  
- Monetisation options: Telegram Stars for digital goods and subs; third-party payment providers also supported. Plan refund flows and dispute handling; Stars can be clawed back on upheld disputes.  
- Attribution and analytics: treat as owned web with UTMs, per-message deep links, and server-side events; pair with Telegram Ads reporting.  
- Common failure modes: treating Telegram like an app store; slow FTUE.  
- KPI gates, 2-week alpha:  
  - Landing to Start ≥ 60 percent  
  - FTUE completion ≥ 70 percent  
  - D1 ≥ 30 percent  
  - First purchase rate ≥ 1.0 percent or subscription attach ≥ 0.5 percent in pay-eligible cohorts  
  - Viral coefficient K ≥ 0.15 where invites exist  
  - Stars refund rate < 2 percent  
- Scale gates (4–6 weeks): D7 ≥ 12 percent; ARPPU trend stable week-over-week.

### Poki (web)
- What matters: staged Player Fit Test then Web Fit Test; monetisation through Poki SDK with rewarded and commercial breaks after testing.  
- Attribution and analytics: Poki SDK events for CTR, conversion to play, first session duration, ad-break readiness.  
- Common failure modes: slow load; heavy bundles; weak thumbnails; long time-to-first-action.  
- KPI gates for Web Fit Test:  
  - Category CTR top quartile in your genre  
  - Conversion to play ≥ 70 percent after first gameplayStart  
  - First session median ≥ 6 minutes in casual or ≥ 10 minutes in arcade/strategy  
  - Time-to-first-interaction ≤ 3 seconds on mid-range laptops  
- Scale gates: featured exposure shows stable engagement and rewardedBreak acceptance ≥ 35 percent without loop drop-off.

### iOS (App Store)
- What matters: measurement via SKAdNetwork and AdAttributionKit; EU alternative distribution and payment options exist under DMA-driven terms, with a Core Technology Fee for certain high-scale choices.  
- Attribution and analytics: SKAN 4 mapping; coarse conversion strategies by window; ASA for branded search; in-app analytics for funnel.  
- Common failure modes: misconfigured SKAN schemas; missing odds disclosures; overstuffed first session.  
- KPI gates for soft launch (mid-core reference ranges):  
  - D1 ≥ 35 percent  
  - D7 ≥ 12 percent  
  - Tutorial completion ≥ 80 percent  
  - Pay conversion ≥ 1.5 percent or subscription trial start ≥ 2.5 percent  
  - ASA cost-per-tap to blended Day-30 ROAS ≥ 70 percent of target with SKAN validated  
  - Compliance: loot box odds disclosed; age ratings correct; ATT prompts only if needed  
- Scale gates: payback ≤ 180 days on blended channels at target margin after App Store fees and any EU fee model.

### Android (Google Play and beyond)
- What matters: Privacy Sandbox changes attribution to on-device APIs; plan for Aggregatable Reports and Attribution Reporting; alternative billing and store options may change fee stacks.  
- Attribution and analytics: Privacy Sandbox for ads; Firebase for product analytics; server-side revenue events.  
- Common failure modes: assuming GAID-based user-level attribution; ignoring sandbox reporting lags.  
- KPI gates for soft launch (mid-core reference ranges):  
  - D1 ≥ 35 percent  
  - D7 ≥ 12 percent  
  - First purchase ≥ 1.2 percent or subscription trial ≥ 2.0 percent  
  - Sandbox-based Day-7 ROAS proxy ≥ 40 percent of target with confidence bands  
  - Store listing experiments yield +10 percent conversion uplift before scale  
- Scale gates: payback ≤ 180 days on blended Android channels; fees modelled per current Play terms and any alternative billing deltas.

### Steam (PC)
- What matters: revenue share tiers step down beyond 10M and 50M lifetime gross; wishlists, followers, demo performance, and Next Fest are key launch drivers.  
- Attribution and analytics: Steamworks reports; page traffic; demo-to-wishlist conversion; festival uplift. Treat wishlist-to-week-one ratios as directional.  
- Common failure modes: late demo; weak capsule art; no festival plan; ignoring A/B.  
- KPI gates:  
  - Pre-launch: ≥ 20,000 wishlists for premium indie, or ≥ 50,000 for ambitious mid-core  
  - Next Fest: demo-to-wishlist conversion ≥ 25 percent; stream concurrence in top quartile of your sub-genre  
  - Launch week: wishlist-to-sale ratio about 0.15× to 0.30×, adjusted for price and Early Access  
- Scale gates: review score ≥ 85 percent positive with ≥ 500 reviews by Day 14; refund rate < 8 percent.

#### Platform quick-reference (pass gates to continue)
| Platform | Pass gates |
|---|---|
| Telegram | Start ≥ 60 percent; FTUE ≥ 70 percent; D1 ≥ 30 percent; First purchase ≥ 1.0 percent or sub attach ≥ 0.5 percent; K ≥ 0.15; refunds < 2 percent |
| Poki | Category CTR top quartile; Conversion to play ≥ 70 percent; First session median ≥ 6–10 minutes; TTFI ≤ 3 s; rewarded acceptance ≥ 35 percent at scale |
| iOS | D1 ≥ 35 percent; D7 ≥ 12 percent; tutorial ≥ 80 percent; pay ≥ 1.5 percent or sub trials ≥ 2.5 percent; ASA D30 ROAS ≥ 70 percent of target; compliance clean |
| Android | D1 ≥ 35 percent; D7 ≥ 12 percent; first purchase ≥ 1.2 percent; Day-7 ROAS proxy ≥ 40 percent of target; listing A/B +10 percent |
| Steam | Wishlists ≥ 20k–50k; Next Fest demo→wishlist ≥ 25 percent; launch wishlist→sale ≈ 0.15×–0.30×; ≥ 85 percent positive reviews |

# Build-this-slide recipes

## Seed: traction slide recipe
- Chart: weekly D1 and D7 lines with annotations for each experiment.  
- Bullets: one learning and one next action in plain English.  
- Footer: cohort sizes; definitions; attribution notes; benchmark comparison in notes.

## Series A: unit economics slide recipe
- Chart: cohort LTV vs CAC by channel with payback bands.  
- Bullets: what moved LTV and what moved CAC.  
- Footer: attribution method by platform; fee assumptions; reporting windows.

## Due Diligence: compliance slide recipe
- Table: platform, policy area, status, owner.  
- Bullets: evidence links to policies and your controls; include Online Safety Act coverage if applicable.

---

# Tutorials and working add-ons

## A. Slide drafting workflow
1) Write the title as the takeaway sentence. If you removed the body, the titles alone should still tell the story end-to-end.  
2) For each slide, list one claim and one proof.  
3) Replace filler with evidence. If you have no evidence, move the claim to the roadmap with a test plan.

## B. Asset checklist per slide
- Cover: logo; working build capture; founder names; contact.  
- Game hook: 15 seconds of real gameplay, not a trailer.  
- Core loop: diagram plus two UI screenshots that show the verbs.  
- Metrics: cohort CSV extract, labelled and dated.  
- GTM: creative taxonomy page and next ten tests.  
- EU fees: one worksheet with fee options and assumptions; dated sources.

## C. Quality control loop
- Run slide-by-slide QA: message clarity; evidence; readability; data labelling; template alignment.  
- Use the 0–5 acceptance rubric per slide and mark pass, minor fixes, or fail.  
- Version the deck and log changes.

## D. Quick Start pack (useful training add-on)
- One page per stage with the 12–15 core slides, a single action line per slide, and a minimal asset list.  
- Time box: 90 minutes to first draft for Seed; 120 minutes for Series A.

## E. Canonical example slides (training add-on)
- Provide three redacted sample slides: Game Hook, Cohort Curves, Payback by Channel. Show titles, captions, labelled axes, and short speaker notes. Include a do vs do-not panel for each.

## F. Fee and policy workbook (appendix add-on)
- A spreadsheet that toggles iOS EU distribution options and Android store routes, feeding a margin bridge slide. Put links, dates, fee definitions, and assumptions at the top.

## G. Headline-as-story storyboard (exercise)
- A 15-title storyboard template so the deck reads as a narrative even without body text.

## H. Designer kit (execution)
- Master slide template with grid, type styles, footer, source line, and numbering.  
- Diagram stencils for loops, funnels, and roadmaps.  
- Chart style file with defaults for lines, bars, waterfalls, and annotation style.

## I. Practice and review protocol
- Rehearsal scripts for a 7-minute and a 12-minute run-through.  
- Red-team checklist for CEO, CPO, CFO, and Growth to flag common failure modes.

---

# Acronyms and definitions (complete)

## Market, finance, investor
- TAM: Total Addressable Market.  
- SAM: Serviceable Available Market.  
- SOM: Serviceable Obtainable Market.  
- LTV: Lifetime Value per user. Sum of expected net revenue per user over time; discount if monthly.  
- CAC: Cost to acquire a user or payer. State which.  
- LTV:CAC: Ratio of value to acquisition cost.  
- Payback period: Earliest day/month cumulative net revenue per user ≥ CAC.  
- ARPU: Average Revenue Per User over a period.  
- ARPPU: Average Revenue Per Paying User.  
- ARPDAU: Average Revenue Per Daily Active User.  
- Gross vs net: Gross is store-side receipts before fees and taxes; Net after platform fees, refunds, ad-net fees.  
- COGS: Cost of Goods Sold (hosting, CDN, payment processing, fraud, support vendors).  
- GM: Gross Margin = (Revenue − COGS) ÷ Revenue.

## Audience, behaviour, retention
- DAU / WAU / MAU: active users by day, week, month.  
- D0, D1, D7, D28, D30: retention checkpoints from install day.  
- Churn: 1 − retention for the cohort over the period.  
- Cohort: users grouped by a shared start attribute.  
- FTUE: First-Time User Experience.  
- Payer rate: period or cumulative; label which.

## UA, advertising, creative
- UA: User Acquisition.  
- CPI / CPA: Cost per install; cost per action.  
- ROAS: Return on ad spend; define window (eg D7, D30).  
- CTR / CVR: Click-through rate; conversion rate. Define the conversion.  
- eCPM: Effective cost per thousand impressions.  
- Ad LTV: Lifetime ad revenue per user.  
- Mediation, waterfall, in-app bidding: ad routing methods.  
- K-factor: Viral coefficient = invites per user × conversion to install.

## Product, monetisation, systems
- IAP / IAA: In-app purchases; in-app advertising.  
- BP: Battle Pass with free and premium tracks.  
- SKU: Stock Keeping Unit; a distinct purchasable.  
- Gacha: Randomised draw with disclosed odds where required.  
- Sources and sinks: Economy inflows and outflows.  
- Session length and cadence: time per session; sessions per day.

## Attribution, privacy, policy
- SKAN: SKAdNetwork, iOS privacy-preserving attribution.  
- AdAttributionKit: Apple’s additional attribution framework.  
- IDFA / ATT: Identifier for Advertisers; App Tracking Transparency prompt.  
- Android Privacy Sandbox: Attribution Reporting API, Topics API, SDK Runtime.  
- DMA / DSA: EU Digital Markets Act / Digital Services Act.  
- OSA: UK Online Safety Act for platforms with UGC or chat.  
- CTF / CTC: Apple EU Core Technology Fee and Commission under alternative terms.

## Technology and operations
- SDK: Software Development Kit.  
- API: Application Programming Interface.  
- CI / CD: Continuous Integration / Continuous Delivery or Deployment.  
- SLA: Service Level Agreement.  
- KPI: Key Performance Indicator.

## Common formulas
- ARPU = revenue in period ÷ active users in period  
- ARPDAU = revenue on day ÷ DAU on day  
- ARPPU = revenue from payers ÷ number of payers in period  
- CAC = acquisition spend ÷ users acquired (define user type)  
- Payback window = earliest day/month cumulative net revenue per user ≥ CAC  
- Payer rate (period) = payers in period ÷ active users in period  
- Retention Dn = percent of a cohort active on day n after install

# Quality checklists and rubrics

## One-minute skim test
- Read only the slide headlines in order. If the story lands cleanly, pass. If not, rewrite headlines.

## Readability checklist
- One idea per slide  
- Minimum 20 pt body text  
- Maximum two evidence bullets  
- Charts labelled with units and dates  
- PDF export under 12–15 MB

## Content completeness gates
- Seed: problem, solution, market, early proof, GTM tests, team, ask.  
- Series A: product stability, growth engine, unit economics, scale plan, hiring, risks.  
- Diligence: full data room index with links.

## Scoring rubric (1–10) for the whole deck
- Quality of narrative  
- Accuracy of claims and sources  
- Detail level versus stage  
- Readability and visual polish  
- Likely retention and recall

# Quick Start front matter

## Seed in 15 slides, 15 minutes first draft
1) Title and promise: one-line purpose, platforms, contact.  
2) Problem or need: two frictions, two desires with proof.  
3) Solution and product: one sentence plus a single annotated screenshot.  
4) Why now: three dated timing drivers and one outcome each.  
5) Market: TAM to SAM to SOM, with bottom-up SOM.  
6) Game hook: 15-second continuous gameplay, genre, camera, session length.  
7) Core loop and two systems: loop diagram, two deepening systems, economy sinks and sources.  
8) Monetisation: first purchase path, SKU ladder, ad strategy if used.  
9) Early metrics or model: D1, D7, D30 and ARPDAU, or LTV model with sensitivity.  
10) Go-to-market: next tests and decision rules with owners.  
11) Distribution advantage: channels, creative angles, creator plan.  
12) Competition: 3 to 5 real substitutes, your wedge.  
13) Team: 4 to 6 leaders with shipped outcomes.  
14) Roadmap and stage-gated milestones: four gates with KPI exits.  
15) The ask: round size, timing, use of proceeds, data room link.

Assets needed now: logo, one gameplay clip, loop diagram, store mockup, one metrics chart or model, a two-line bio per leader, a milestone timeline.

## Series A in 15 slides, 120 minutes first draft
1) Title and current state: installs, MAU, revenue run rate.  
2) Narrative of progress: prototype to now with wins tied to experiments.  
3) Product deep dive: live-ops cadence, economy stability.  
4) Traction overview: D1, D7, D30, ARPDAU, payer rate, refunds.  
5) Cohorts and retention: curves by source and platform.  
6) Monetisation deep dive: SKU ladder, funnels, ad contribution.  
7) Unit economics: LTV by cohort and channel, CAC by channel, payback with sensitivity.  
8) GTM engine: channel mix, creative taxonomy, cadence, creator programmes.  
9) Tech and operations: build pipeline, analytics, experiment framework, compliance.  
10) Roadmap and scale plan: new markets, content cadence, infra.  
11) Team for scale: recent hires and gaps mapped to risks.  
12) Financials: drivers, burn, runway, scenario plan.  
13) EU fee and distribution impact: iOS EU options, Android choices, margin bridge.  
14) Risks and mitigations: five specific risks with owners.  
15) The ask: round size, timing, data room link.

# Universal narrative spine and slide count policy

## Narrative beats investors expect
Purpose, Why now, Market, Product and core loop, Business model and economy, Distribution and GTM, Competition, Team, Roadmap, Financials and use of funds, Risks, The Ask.

## Slide count and pacing
- Live Seed or Series A: 10 to 15 slides for the core narrative.  
- Send-ahead PDF: 12 to 18 slides for the core, with appendix for tables and cohorts.  
- Due Diligence: 15 to 25 slide overview with a linked data room.

# Seed deck tutorial: full slide-by-slide build

For each slide: Objective, What to show, Why it matters, Inputs and assets, Visual spec, Quality checks, Pitfalls.

1) Cover  
Objective: set promise and context fast.  
What to show: studio name, one-line promise, platform focus, founders, contact, one in-engine image or 5–10 second loop.  
Why it matters: frames quality and category.  
Inputs: logo, gameplay capture, contact.  
Visual spec: 16:9 at 1920×1080, safe margins 40 px, grid, Title ≥ 40 pt, Headings ≥ 28 pt, Body ≥ 20 pt, Labels ≥ 16 pt. Recommended Body ≥ 24 pt if space allows.  
Checks: legal-cleared image, readable title.  
Pitfalls: concept art not representative of play.

2) Why now  
Objective: show timing edge.  
What to show: three dated drivers and one outcome each.  
Why it matters: investors back timing.  
Inputs: two to three data points with dates.  
Visual spec: one chart or mini timeline.  
Checks: tie each driver to CPI, watch-time, payer rate, or distribution access.  
Pitfalls: vague trends, stale data.

3) Opportunity  
Objective: quantify realistic upside.  
What to show: TAM, SAM, SOM with bottom-up SOM and one reachability line.  
Why it matters: aligns ambition to execution.  
Inputs: market numbers with dates, peer comps.  
Visual spec: bars labelled with units and dates.  
Checks: SOM defendable, not a flat percent of TAM.  
Pitfalls: double-counted markets.

4) Problem and player insight  
Objective: prove understanding of the player.  
What to show: two frictions, two desires, each with a clip or quote, audience and play occasion.  
Why it matters: accurate insight predicts retention.  
Inputs: playtest notes, short reels.  
Visual spec: two tiles, captions ≤ 15 words.  
Checks: sub-genre specific.  
Pitfalls: generic personas.

5) The game: 15-second hook  
Objective: communicate the core in one breath.  
What to show: one sentence, 15-second continuous gameplay, genre, camera, primary interaction, average session length.  
Why it matters: spark excitement with truth.  
Inputs: capture from a working build.  
Visual spec: 1080p MP4, ≤ 15 MB, HUD visible if clarifying.  
Checks: real input feedback visible.  
Pitfalls: teaser CG that hides inputs.

6) Core loop and systems  
Objective: show how fun compounds into retention and spend.  
What to show: loop diagram with 3 to 5 verbs, two deepening systems, sinks and sources.  
Why it matters: loops generate economics.  
Inputs: loop schematic, economy list, UI shots.  
Visual spec: one loop schematic, two callouts.  
Checks: loop fits session length, systems are additive.  
Pitfalls: bloat before soft launch.

7) Distribution advantage  
Objective: show access beyond spend.  
What to show: channels, creative angles, community and creators, any placements, table of channel, CPI target, expected scale.  
Why it matters: distribution is a moat.  
Inputs: creator list, community plan, placement prospects.  
Visual spec: table ≤ 6 rows.  
Checks: at least one non-paid lever and a test plan.  
Pitfalls: assuming paid UA coverage at modelled CPI.

8) Monetisation model  
Objective: show value exchange and pricing logic.  
What to show: pillars like cosmetics, gacha, BP, price bands, store mockups, ad strategy if used, guardrails against pay-to-win.  
Why it matters: trust drives payer rate.  
Inputs: SKU ladder, price points, bundles, UX wires.  
Visual spec: one mockup, one table.  
Checks: first purchase path is obvious, sinks sized to cadence.  
Pitfalls: copying top grossing store without fit.

9) Early metrics or model  
Objective: anchor on data or be explicit with assumptions.  
What to show: tested D1, D7, D30, ARPDAU, payer rate, first-purchase time by source, or a transparent LTV model with sensitivity ranges and benchmarks.  
Why it matters: investors underwrite to curves.  
Inputs: cohort tables, model sheet.  
Visual spec: one lead chart, small cohort table, axes labelled, units and dates visible.  
Checks: no blended cohorts, sensitivity ± 20 percent on key drivers.  
Pitfalls: cherry-picked cohorts.

10) Go-to-market  
Objective: show the first 180-day learning plan.  
What to show: test geos, creative testing cadence, community beats, creator plan, referral mechanics, PR moments, measurement per channel.  
Why it matters: speed to learning reduces capital.  
Inputs: calendar, creative backlog, test matrices, Discord plan, SKAN schema mapping, Android Sandbox plan.  
Visual spec: one timetable, one attribution method box.  
Checks: decision rules and owners, stop rules documented.  
Pitfalls: long launch with no gates.

11) Competitive landscape  
Objective: position against real substitutes.  
What to show: 3 to 5 comps and your wedge in fun, distribution, or economics.  
Why it matters: shows clarity of field.  
Inputs: feature grid, revenue ranks.  
Visual spec: simple 2×2 or comparison table, three callouts.  
Checks: wedge visible in loop, not only brand.  
Pitfalls: giant grids.

12) Team  
Objective: de-risk execution with relevant wins.  
What to show: 4 to 6 leaders, two lines each tied to shipped titles or scaled live ops, advisory board only if hands on.  
Why it matters: pre-seed and seed are team bets.  
Inputs: bios, shipped games, coverage map.  
Visual spec: consistent headshots, tiles aligned.  
Checks: coverage for loop, economy, live ops, data, UA.  
Pitfalls: long bios, celebrity advisors without time.

13) Roadmap and stage-gated milestones  
Objective: align capital to outcomes.  
What to show: past proof with dates, next four gates with exit criteria and KPIs, for example First Playable, Closed Alpha, Soft-launch 1 and 2, Global Candidate.  
Why it matters: investors commit to gates.  
Inputs: milestone plan, KPI targets, risk owners.  
Visual spec: timeline with KPIs beside each gate.  
Checks: measurable KPIs such as D1, D7, FTUE, payback.  
Pitfalls: vague words like polish.

14) Financial plan snapshot  
Objective: present burn and runway tied to plan.  
What to show: 18 to 24 month budget by function, hiring tranches, third parties, infra, UA runway, cash burn, months runway, unit-economics summary such as target LTV by cohort and payback.  
Why it matters: validates ask size and survivability.  
Inputs: headcount plan, vendor quotes, UA assumptions.  
Visual spec: one burn line, one unit-economics table.  
Checks: month-by-month reconciliation, hiring matches milestones, UA after retention gates.  
Pitfalls: flat headcount, UA spend too early.

15) EU distribution and fees summary  
Objective: reflect EU realities.  
What to show: iOS EU options and fee components, Android fee differences where applicable, comparison table, note that the full fee model is in the appendix workbook.  
Why it matters: net revenue depends on choices.  
Inputs: EU terms references, your fee worksheet.  
Visual spec: two columns, footnotes and dates.  
Checks: totals reconcile to model, assumptions noted.  
Pitfalls: mixing gross and net.

16) Risks and mitigations  
Objective: build trust by naming risks.  
What to show: top 5 risks across product, UA, tech, compliance, team, one line mitigation and owner each.  
Why it matters: speeds diligence.  
Inputs: risk register, owners, contingency costs.  
Visual spec: five rows, owner and next check column.  
Checks: specific, testable.  
Pitfalls: clichés.

17) The ask  
Objective: make it easy to progress.  
What to show: round size, instrument, timing, lead or committed if any, use of proceeds, data room link, contact.  
Why it matters: sets the next step.  
Inputs: terms, timeline, data room.  
Visual spec: large contact line.

# Series A deck tutorial: full slide-by-slide build

1) Cover: consistent identity and current state.  
2) Why now update: platform and market motion since Seed.  
3) Traction summary: installs, DAU or MAU, payers, revenue mix, top geos, lead curve.  
4) Product deep dive: live-ops cadence, economy sinks and sources, ARPPU stability.  
5) Cohorts and retention: D1, D7, D28 or D30 by source and platform, no blends.  
6) Monetisation deep dive: SKU ladder, first-purchase funnel, price tests, ad stack, refunds.  
7) Unit economics: LTV by cohort and channel, CAC by channel, LTV:CAC, payback windows with sensitivity, attribution method labelled.  
8) GTM engine: channel mix, creative taxonomy, volume, win-rate, refresh cadence, creator programmes.  
9) Technology and operations: build pipeline, analytics, A/B framework, live-ops tooling, compliance posture.  
10) Roadmap and scale plan: new markets, content cadence, feature bets, infra scale.  
11) Team for scale: upgraded coverage, open roles mapped to risks.  
12) Financials: revenue, gross margin drivers, burn, runway, scenario drivers, fee and policy impacts.  
13) EU distribution and fees impact: iOS EU options and components, Android terms where applicable, one margin bridge from gross to net.  
14) Risks and mitigations: five risks, owners, mitigations, checkpoint dates.  
15) The ask: round size, timing, data room link, hiring tranche table reference.

# Due Diligence deck: structure and contents

1) Executive summary with deep links.  
2) Company and legal: entities, cap table, options, contracts, licences, IP assignments.  
3) Product and roadmap: design docs, live-ops calendars, feature backlogs, pipelines, release process.  
4) Data and analytics: event taxonomy, cohort exports by geo, source, platform, version, retention and revenue curves, attribution method per cut, SKAN schema, Privacy Sandbox test summaries.  
5) Go-to-market: UA test logs, channel performance, creative taxonomy and results, creator programmes, community ops, store listing experiments.  
6) Financials: historical P&L, cash flow, forecasts, budget by function, vendor schedules, UA spend logs, margin bridges that reflect platform fees.  
7) Technology: architecture, SDK list, CI pipeline, security, compliance notes, data retention and privacy.  
8) People: bios, hiring plan, contractors, compensation bands, coverage gaps.  
9) Risks and compliance: risk register, mitigations, policy alignment, Online Safety Act posture if UGC or chat, age assurance plan and vendor, moderation workflows, EU DMA choices and fee rationale.  
10) Appendices: store pages, reviews, CS tags, platform communications, legal correspondence.

# Visual and Fidelity guide: full spec

Foundations  
- Canvas: 16:9 at 1920×1080. Safe margins 40 px. 12-column grid or simple 4-column grid with 24 px gutters.  
- Palette: one primary, one secondary, one highlight, two neutrals. Limit categories in a chart to six.  
- Type: single sans-serif family. Title ≥ 40 pt, Headings ≥ 28 pt, Body ≥ 20 pt, Labels ≥ 16 pt. Recommend Body ≥ 24 pt where space allows. Line spacing 1.15 to 1.3.  
- Contrast: meet WCAG AA.  
- Density: one message per slide, three to five short lines, one primary graphic.

Imagery and video  
- Gameplay: working build, 1080p, show input and feedback. Hook clip 15 seconds.  
- Compression: H.264, ≤ 15 MB per clip. Static images 150–200 DPI, UI as PNG, backgrounds as JPEG under 400 KB.  
- Framing: include HUD when it clarifies mechanics.

Charts and tables  
- Bars, lines, waterfalls, cohort curves, funnels. Avoid pies.  
- Axes start at zero unless annotated. Always label units, currency, dates.  
- Annotate one insight on the chart. Keep gridlines faint.  
- Tables in core deck ≤ 6 rows by 4 columns. Larger tables go to appendix.

Slide patterns by purpose  
- Cover, hook, loop, market, monetisation, metrics, team, risks. See Seed and Series A recipes.

Animation and motion  
- Simple appear or fade, 200 to 300 ms, maximum two per slide. Export final static state to PDF.

Accessibility and readability  
- Colour distinctions must also have labels or patterns.  
- No text over busy imagery without a dark or light overlay.  
- Provide concise alt text in speaker notes for key visuals.

Brand and UI discipline  
- Title top-left, source line bottom-right, slide number bottom-centre.  
- No decorative icons.  
- Do not mix rounded and sharp shapes unless it mirrors in-game UI.

File hygiene  
- Master template only. Title, content, divider, appendix masters defined before build.  
- Versioning: DeckName_vMajor.Minor_Date. Include a change log slide.  
- Exports: PDF ≤ 12–15 MB with embedded fonts. Provide a link to the live deck for meetings.

QA checklist per slide  
- Message clear as a title sentence.  
- Evidence present and dated or sourced.  
- Body text ≥ 20 pt, ideally 24 pt.  
- One primary graphic.  
- Units, time bases, axes and sources labelled.  
- Aligned to grid, consistent footers and numbering.

Acceptance rubric 0 to 5  
- 5 investor-ready, 4 minor tweaks, 3 needs revision, 2 major issues, 1 unusable.

# Evidence, metrics, and references for games
Use retention and monetisation bands from current industry benchmarks as context only. Treat medians as directional and calibrate by genre and geo. Log sources and dates in the evidence table.

# Platform annex: channel-specific guidance and KPI gates

How to use: copy the experiment template, run a 2 to 4 week test, decide with pass or iterate gates.

Experiment design template  
- Objective, audience and geo, entry points, tracking plan, creative set, budget caps, success gates, next action.

Telegram Mini Apps  
- What matters: distribution via channels, groups, bot discovery, deep links, Telegram Ads. Mini Apps are JS Web Apps with APIs for auth, payments, fullscreen, theming, device capabilities. Stars enable in-Telegram purchases and subscriptions.  
- Monetisation: Stars for digital goods and subs, third-party payments as applicable. Plan refund flows and disputes.  
- Attribution: treat as owned web with UTMs and server-side events, plus Telegram Ads reporting.  
- Failure modes: treating Telegram like an app store, slow FTUE.  
- KPI gates, 2-week alpha: Start ≥ 60 percent, FTUE ≥ 70 percent, D1 ≥ 30 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.0 percent or subscription attach ≥ 0.5 percent, viral K ≥ 0.15, refunds < 2 percent.  
- Scale gates, 4 to 6 weeks: D7 ≥ 12 percent, stable ARPPU trend.

Poki web  
- What matters: Player Fit Test then Web Fit Test. Monetisation through Poki SDK with rewarded and commercial breaks after testing.  
- Attribution: Poki SDK events for CTR, conversion to play, first session duration, ad-break readiness.  
- Failure modes: heavy bundles, weak thumbnails, long time-to-first-action.  
- KPI gates: category CTR top quartile, conversion to play ≥ 70 percent, first session median ≥ 6 minutes casual or ≥ 10 minutes strategy, time-to-first-interaction ≤ 3 seconds.  
- Scale gates: featured exposure stable, rewarded acceptance ≥ 35 percent without loop drop-off.

iOS App Store  
- What matters: SKAdNetwork and AdAttributionKit. EU alternative terms introduce fee choices that affect margin.  
- Attribution: SKAN 4 mapping, conversion strategies by window, Apple Search Ads for branded search, in-app analytics.  
- Failure modes: misconfigured SKAN, missing odds disclosures, heavy first session.  
- KPI gates for soft launch mid-core: D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent, tutorial completion ≥ 80 percent, pay conversion ≥ 1.5 percent or subscription trials ≥ 2.5 percent, ASA Day-30 ROAS ≥ 70 percent of target with SKAN validated, compliance clean.  
- Scale gates: payback ≤ 180 days on blended channels at target margin after fees.

Android  
- What matters: Privacy Sandbox replaces cross-party IDs. Factor reporting cadence and windowing into tests.  
- Attribution: Privacy Sandbox for ads, Firebase for analytics, server-side revenue events.  
- Failure modes: assuming GAID user-level attribution, ignoring reporting lags.  
- KPI gates mid-core: D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.2 percent or subscription trials ≥ 2.0 percent, Day-7 ROAS proxy ≥ 40 percent of target with confidence bands, listing A/B uplift ≥ 10 percent before scale.  
- Scale gates: payback ≤ 180 days, fees modelled correctly.

Steam  
- What matters: wishlist velocity, demo performance, Next Fest presence, revenue share steps at 10M and 50M lifetime gross.  
- Attribution: Steamworks reports, page traffic, demo-to-wishlist conversion, festival uplift.  
- Failure modes: late demo, weak capsule art, no A/B.  
- KPI gates: pre-launch wishlists ≥ 20k to 50k by scope, Next Fest demo-to-wishlist ≥ 25 percent, launch wishlist-to-sale about 0.15× to 0.30× adjusted for price and Early Access.  
- Scale gates: review score ≥ 85 percent positive with ≥ 500 reviews by Day 14, refund rate < 8 percent.

Platform quick-reference  
Telegram: pass if Start ≥ 60 percent, FTUE ≥ 70 percent, D1 ≥ 30 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.0 percent or sub attach ≥ 0.5 percent, K ≥ 0.15, refunds < 2 percent.  
Poki: pass if category CTR top quartile, conversion ≥ 70 percent, median first session ≥ 6–10 minutes, TTFI ≤ 3 seconds, rewarded acceptance ≥ 35 percent at scale.  
iOS: pass if D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent, tutorial ≥ 80 percent, pay ≥ 1.5 percent or trials ≥ 2.5 percent, ASA D30 ROAS ≥ 70 percent of target, compliance clean.  
Android: pass if D1 ≥ 35 percent, D7 ≥ 12 percent, first purchase ≥ 1.2 percent, D7 ROAS proxy ≥ 40 percent of target, listing A/B +10 percent.  
Steam: pass if wishlists ≥ 20k–50k, Next Fest demo→wishlist ≥ 25 percent, launch wishlist→sale ≈ 0.15×–0.30×, ≥ 85 percent positive reviews.

# Build-this-slide recipes

Seed traction slide  
- Chart: weekly D1 and D7 with annotations at experiment dates.  
- Bullets: one learning, one next action.  
- Footer: cohort sizes, definitions, attribution method, benchmark reference.

Series A unit economics slide  
- Chart: cohort LTV vs CAC by channel with payback bands.  
- Bullets: what moved LTV, what moved CAC.  
- Footer: attribution method by platform, fee assumptions, reporting windows.

Diligence compliance slide  
- Table: platform, policy area, status, owner.  
- Bullets: evidence links and controls, Online Safety Act coverage if applicable.

# Tutorials and working add-ons

Slide drafting workflow  
1) Title the takeaway as a sentence.  
2) One claim, one proof.  
3) No proof means move the claim to roadmap with a test plan.

Asset checklist per slide  
- Cover: logo, gameplay capture, founder names, contact.  
- Hook: 15 seconds real gameplay.  
- Loop: diagram plus two UI screenshots.  
- Metrics: cohort CSV extract labelled and dated.  
- GTM: creative taxonomy page and next ten tests.  
- EU fees: worksheet with options and assumptions, dated sources.

Quality control loop  
- Per slide QA: message clarity, evidence, readability, data labelling, template alignment.  
- Use the 0 to 5 acceptance rubric and log pass, minor fixes, or fail.  
- Version the deck and keep a change log.

# Evidence table template

Use this in the appendix and keep it current.

Columns  
- Claim text  
- Slide number  
- Source title and link or file path  
- Source type and date  
- Method notes or caveats  
- Confidence 1 to 5  
- Owner  
- Next refresh date

# Fee and policy workbook outline

Purpose  
- Provide toggles for iOS EU distribution choices and Android store routes with an output sheet that feeds a margin bridge slide.

Sheets  
1) Inputs  
- App platforms, geo, fee choices, billing route, refund assumptions, tax placeholder.  
2) iOS EU fees  
- Variables for standard terms vs alternative terms, fee percentages, thresholds.  
3) Android routes  
- Default Play terms, alternative billing adjustments, alt store estimates.  
4) Revenue and fees  
- Gross by platform and geo, fee rows, net revenue.  
5) Margin bridge output  
- Bars from gross to net per platform and a combined view for the slide.

Instruction  
- Use named ranges only. Add date and source notes at the top of Inputs. Link the margin bridge chart to the output sheet.

# Cohort and payback kit

CSV schema for cohort exports  
- install_date, platform, channel, geo, app_version, cohort_size, day_0_active, day_1_active, day_7_active, day_30_active, day_0_rev, day_1_rev, day_7_rev, day_30_rev, cumulative_rev_day_30, cac, attribution_method

Excel or Python recipe outline  
- Retention D1, D7, D30 = active ÷ cohort_size.  
- ARPU by day = revenue ÷ active or ÷ cohort_size as noted.  
- LTV at day n = cumulative_rev_day_n ÷ cohort_size.  
- Payback day = first day where LTV ≥ CAC.  
- Channel view = group by channel and platform, compute LTV, CAC, payback, and sensitivity bands ± 20 percent.

Chart style  
- Lines for retention by cohort, stacked bars for margin bridge, consistent fonts and label sizes, axes labelled with units and dates.

# Canonical example slides

Example 1: Game Hook  
- Title: Build, raid, and outsmart rivals in ten-minute sessions.  
- Visual: 15-second continuous clip that shows input and response, HUD visible.  
- Bullets: Genre and camera, sessions per day, platform focus.  
- Footer: Build version and capture date.  
Do not: use a CG teaser or hide input feedback.

Example 2: Cohort Curves  
- Title: Retention stabilises above target bands after onboarding fix.  
- Visual: Lines for D1, D7, D30 by install week and platform.  
- Bullets: Week X onboarding cut lifted D1 by 4 points, new loop cadence improved D7.  
- Footer: cohort definitions, attribution method, unit and date labels.  
Do not: blend cohorts or omit method notes.

Example 3: Payback by Channel  
- Title: iOS search and Android video creatives pay back within 120 to 150 days.  
- Visual: Payback chart per channel with sensitivity bands.  
- Bullets: What moved LTV up, what reduced CAC, next test.  
- Footer: fee assumptions, attribution window, last refresh date.  
Do not: present a single blended ratio.

# Acronyms and definitions

Market, finance, investor  
- TAM, SAM, SOM, LTV, CAC, LTV:CAC, Payback period, ARPU, ARPPU, ARPDAU, Gross vs Net, COGS, GM.

Audience, behaviour, retention  
- DAU, WAU, MAU, D0, D1, D7, D28, D30, Churn, Cohort, FTUE, Payer rate.

UA, advertising, creative  
- UA, CPI, CPA, ROAS, CTR, CVR, eCPM, Ad LTV, Mediation, Waterfall, In-app bidding, K-factor.

Product, monetisation, systems  
- IAP, IAA, BP, SKU, Gacha, Sources and sinks, Session length and cadence.

Attribution, privacy, policy  
- SKAN, AdAttributionKit, IDFA, ATT, Android Privacy Sandbox, DMA, DSA, OSA, CTF, CTC.

Technology and operations  
- SDK, API, CI, CD, SLA, KPI.

Common formulas  
- ARPU = revenue in period ÷ active users in period  
- ARPDAU = revenue on day ÷ DAU on day  
- ARPPU = revenue from payers ÷ number of payers in period  
- CAC = acquisition spend ÷ users acquired  
- Payback window = first day or month where cumulative net revenue per user ≥ CAC  
- Payer rate (period) = payers in period ÷ active users in period  
- Retention Dn = percent of cohort active on day n

# Checklists and rubrics

One-minute skim test  
- Headlines alone tell a coherent story.

Readability checklist  
- One idea per slide, Body ≥ 20 pt, ideally 24 pt, maximum two evidence bullets, charts labelled with units and dates, PDF under 12–15 MB.

Content completeness gates  
- Seed: problem, solution, market, proof, GTM tests, team, ask.  
- Series A: product stability, growth engine, unit economics, scale plan, hiring, risks.  
- Diligence: full data room index with links.

Scoring rubric 1 to 10  
- Quality of narrative, Accuracy of claims and sources, Detail level versus stage, Readability and visual polish, Likely retention and recall.

Day 0 outline, Day 1 draft, Day 3 critique pass, Day 5 polish. Time-box Seed to 90 minutes, Series A to 120 minutes for first complete drafts.
